<UserId.>113548220739591435574<//UserId.><user_name>Anton</user_name><Date>1511446317696</Date><Rate>5< /Rate>< text>
Absolutely incredible hike(s). Trails are shaped like heart üíì with additional trail splitting the heart in halfs and trailhead located at the bottom of the heart. You can hike right side (6mi) only or left side (7mi) only or whole heart (13-14mi). If you do right half that go counterclockwise for easier hike and clockwise for more intense hike. And if you do left side and then go clockwise for easier hike and counterclockwise for more intense.
And one more VERY important point: to get to trailhead you will need to go on dirt road and in couple places you might need people to get out of the car to get better clearance. But if you go slow and pay attention then this dirt should not be a problem.</text>

Red Mountain Loop- a fairly easy overnighter but one of the only places I've heard of where you can actually sleep among the giant Sequoias, even the groves themselves are worth the day hike (plus views of Kings Canyon). There are some excellent little established sites for camping if you keep hiking towards Big Spring. Crowds at the entrances of both loops, but hiking just a few miles yields decent solitude.< /text>

<username>Estella Escalante</username><gmap_id>0x80956ef121d3fd39:0x67849ee9e1441ac</gmap_id><UserId.>105713081424290052857< /UserId.><rate>5< /rate>< Review>
Hiked the Sugar Bowl then up Redwood Creek as a loop through this area by suggestion of a Forest Ranger. Ended up climbing a mountain with the most amazing views but the best part is the many groves of trees and solitude. Once you get to the furthest point before going down to the creek you see Sequoias as big as the tourist areas.  There is bear poop along the trail so I‚Äôm sure there would be a lot of sightings. Some parts of the trail are overgrown with poison oak and ivy present so wear long pants if you are sensitive. I would hike this again but use the Hart trail on the way back.<//Review>

Visited the SmileShop in Redwood City today.   What a great experience.  The team working there were very nice and welcoming.

After filling in some personal info on their iPad, it was off to another office for the 3D image of my teeth and smile.  Quisa, a dental assistant, was efficient, friendly and fast in doing the image.  She answered all my questions.  The technology is amazing.

Once the 3D image was complete, we talked about next steps and the payment plan ($1895 or $250 down and $85 month for 24 months).  This is about the third of the cost for regular braces.  And on average, takes about 6 months of wearing aligners all the time except when eating and drinking.

I am not yet sure that I will order the aligners but I highly recommend checking out the SmileShop in Redwood City.<//Text>

<Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Text>
I had lunch in Cathedral City with a friend of mine and was excited about how good the food was in the restaurant. I had the meatballs in a bowl and they were light and fluffy and well seasoned. My friend had the spaghetti and it looked fresh and inviting. The feel and taste of the food brought back memories of Old Italy in New York and their restaurant is rustic. They have bistro tables in the bar for those of us with issues getting out of those beastly low chairs. I left happy and talked my partner into ordering a pizza from them for our dinner that night. He got a ham & pineapple pizza and I got their #2 Calzone. When they arrived and we got a look at them the crust was mushy and wet as though it had not been in a hot enough oven. I tired to make excuses like it must of sat on the line before you picked it up, but he had  to wait for it. Then I tried well it must have been the box and the ride home. But, being a chef I know when something isn't cooked correctly. We were highly disappointed with their take away pizza and calzone. I ate half of mine and just heated the other half up in the oven for lunch. Admittedly with a little more heat it tasted much better and wasn't as mushy as the first go a-round. I'll hesitate ordering a take out pizza/calzone from them in the future. I'll visit for lunch and see if they can kick-start this relationship again. They have been a cornerstone of the community for 40 years I believe I read. Common guys! Pay attention and don't take advantage of the love we give you.<//Text>

<Rate>2</Rate>< Review>
Disappointing is an understatement. It was a Saturday and I was in urgent need of a trim. Unfortunately my regular barber was unavailable this weekend and I had to settle for an alternate. One stylist with a walk in basis is how this barbershop was functioning on Saturday evening which was just not efficient, but I decided to wait and take the plunge.

I requested for a fade on my sides with a one and two clipper while the top to have the hair length from a three clipper with more hair in the front for styling. Nothing was achieved . The haircut was bland and for 30$ there was absolutely no styling, no fading , or any sharpness in the cut. Might as well gone to supercut or similar.

The other thing which irked me was the way the clippers, scissors, brushes, etc. were not sanitized between clients. They are all kept in a bunch on the table behind the barber who takes and uses as needed. I had a beard trim along with the haircut and hair from the clipper went into my eyes, only god knows whose hair that was. Also, my beard trim resulted in removal of most of my beard, which was clearly adding salt to an already badly injured wound.

Wish they have more barbers/stylists or provide appointments which would be more efficient. Also, wish sanitary standards are not compromised!

2 stars only for the hot towel at the end.

Not going to head here again but thankfully it's just hair and it will grow back!<//Review>

< Review>
Food: 4 Stars
Ambiance: 4 Stars (Casual but clean)
Service: 2 Stars...the owner is really friendly and attentive but I've found on numerous occasions that the staff are just slow and somewhat oblivious. Despite the fact that it's a small cafe and not too many tables to serve, consistently see that they seat people slowly, miss bringing menus, don't refill coffee or water...the list goes on and on.

Would I come back? Yes, for the food and the owner and the fact that it's the only spot within walking distance of where I get my oil changes and tire rotations.

However, I really wish the owner would address the staff's lackadaisical attitude. In a way I can't fault the owner since it seems it's just hard to get good help these days.</Review>

< Review>
Patio Coffee Shop is a favorite of locals.  It's not fancy, but it's comfortable and the people are always friendly, staff and patrons alike.  I appreciate that it's one of a kind and not a knock-off of every other coffee shop around.  Parking on 25th can be dicey at shopping hours, but there's always plenty on the side streets. The restaurants and retail shops here project a similar idiosyncratic but quality character.  25th Avenue is one of San Mateo's oldest and most genuine neighborhoods, with a warm ambience that reflects the homeyness of this part of town.</Review>
